REPUBLIC OF KEYA
MICRO- AND SMALL ENTERPRISE TRAINING AND TECHNOLOGY PROJECT
PILOT INCUBATOR (INFRASTRUCTURE) PROGRAM
A. Rationale
1.    In Kenya, the Government has not been successful in providing infrastructure required for
the informal sector development because of lack of consultation with end users, ownershi,
problems and other disincentives. Although many private landlords are able to provide sites and
services, this is too expensive for Jua Kalis to afford and as a result, squatting abounds. The
objective of this component is to make the appropriate work places affordable to viable Jua Kali
businesses. To this end, the project would: a) identify and secure land for the Jua Kali sector; b)
develop the infrastructure on selected sites; and c) institute a management system for allocating
and managing the land and facilities.
2.    Security of land tenure and access to appropriate infrastructure -- access roads, water and
drainage, and electricity in the sites - are crucial to the development of the Jua Kali sector.
Land tenure, as a collateral, makes credit accessible to entrepreneurs and gives incentive to invest
in capital, develop sites and advance technology. The lack of basic infrastructure is a barrier to
the improvement of technology, e.g. shifting from hand to power tools. Consumers are also
discouraged to purchase Jua Kali goods due to the difficulties in reaching the sites caused by the
abserce of access road and footpaths.
B. Security of Work Sites
3.    Plot Location. Size and Numbeis of Work Places: Acquiring land is a fundamental
requirement for building infrastructure. A number of sites have already been identified and
allocated by the local Commissioner of Lands (COL) to MRTT&T. The land will be contributed
by the Government without charge. The infrastructure program would be carried out, on a pilot
basis, on sites in Mombasa and Kisumu respectively. In two towns, a total of approximately 500
work places of different sizes would be developed: plot sizes varying from 6X6 meters, 6XI0,
1OX16 and upwards, depending on the activity to be carried out. An estimated 170 work places
would be created at Mombasa on two sites and 330 work places at Kisumu on two sites, to
accommodate a total of about 3000 workers by the end of the project.
4.    Ownership and Payments to be Levied: The infrastructure component will be a DiLot
mini-incubator exercise based on the principle of 'site and service', with the full participation of
entrepreneur operators. Two methods of ownership by Jua Kali operators are proposed: in
Mombasa some sites would be acquired by individual operators under a standard lease
arrangement (33, 66, and 99 years), arranged through the local Jua Kali Association - who
receives a Letter of Allotment from the Conmissioner of Lands (sample copies contained in the
implementation volume) initially - and where land rates and transfer fee are paid to the
Commissioner of Lands by the Association who later levy a charge on the operator when
individual title is handed over. A further charge to be levied is land tax payable to the
Commissioner of Lands each year by the title holder. Rates, transfer fee and land tax vary
according to location and area of land and are calculated on a standard formula (see para. 19). If
an operator wishes to sell his/her building and contents after two to three years occupancy, the
sale would go to a co-member of the Jua Kali Association and it is recommended that MRTT&T



93                            ANNEX 8
Page 2 of 11
notify the Commissioner of Lands that a caveat be included in each operators title ensuring that
the transfer of ownership will be to a bone fide/long term member of the Association. The
remaining sites at Mombasa and all sites at Kisumu will be leased (10 years, renewable) to
operators through the Jua Kali Association, and where MRTT&T receive the Letter of Allotment
to the land title from the Commissioner of Lands and where no costs for land rates and transfer
fee are involved. However, a charge for land tax is still levied on the Jua Kaii operator.
5.    Site Location Criteria: Each site will be located considering the following criteria: i) near
to an area of heavy human traffic; ii) near to or off a good trunk road and easily accessible; and,
iii) has direct access to essential services such as electricity, water, drainage, storm water disposal
and refuse collection facilities. Sites will be under the over all charge of a Jua Kali Association
who would be responsible for its future operation and maintenance, its transparent selection of
operators (with representatives of MRTT&T, the Local Authority, Jua Kali Association, etc.),
collection of rents/payments, maintenance and service charges from operators, training of artisans
and laborers in construction techniques, distribution of materials, overall supervision and day-to-
day management procedures (see attached selection survey rating sct.edule).
6.    Tenure Arrangement: In terms of the tenure arrangement, this project proposes a
combination of access; long-term lease at Kisumu, and ownership and long term lease at
Mombasa, based on the size of business. Jua Kalis about to graduate who can afford the cost of
leasing and ongoing maintenance cost and charges would be granted ownership, while others
would be under a leasehold arrangement. Common facilities such as public toilets, Jua Kali office
and materials store/exhibition space would be owned and managed by the Jua Kali Associations.
7.    OwnershiM: Unider the "ownership" approach, where the MRTT&T has the allotment, the
work places would be allocated to individual Jua Kalis on long leases at completion of the
infrastructure construction. They would be priced at market rates with repayments on a "tenant
purchase" basis. The common areas and facilities would be managed and maintained by the Jua
Kali Association and the related arrangement, e.g. fees and service charges, would be prepared.
Repayments would be collected by the Jua Kali Association. The security would be the title to
the work place.
8.    Leasing Arrangement: For micro Jua Kali businesses, the work places would be rented
under a leasehold arrangement. The lease period would be 10 years and would be renewable.
The type of business to be carried on the premises would be specified and would not be able to be
altered without the permission of management. Sub-letting would be only allowed if the
leaseholder also works on the premises. This would enable larger work places to be shared.
Absentee landlords would be prohibited.
C. Infrastructure Provision
9.    Infrastructure. Buildings and Services to be Provided: This component is similar to a site-
and-service program. Each of the work places would have individual water, sewerage, and
electrical connection. In addition, the sites would be provided with access roads, public toilets,
and drainage. These facilities will be designed in close consultation with the users. Each site
would also have an office for the Jua Kali Associations use and a store for building material
distribution during the construction of the individual operators sheds over the first three years of
the project. After which time, this store would be converted to a permanent exhibition center
where improved technology could be taught to the immediate and surrounding Jua Kali operators.



94                              ANNEX 8
Page 3 of 11
Given that Jua Kalis are skilled artisans, a large part of the construction of the operator sheds will
be done by manual labor of the members (self-help) as well as by paid full-time workers.
Technical assistance and supervision on the construction would be provided by contracted
consultant services. The local authorities would  't be involved in the project except for the
provision of some services during and after the construction, such as garbage collection. Building
materials for operator sheds would be provided through the Credit and distributed to the operators
by the Jua Kali Association. Operators would essentially be responsible for constructing their
own structures on a force account basis, however, some controls would be exercised to ensure
that appropriate construction techniques and materials are used, training in construction methods
provided and si -ervision given. Typical stapdard layouts for the small scale business operator
would be prepa.ed prior to effectiveness. These would consider different layouts and structures
for different operations which could include animal food production, furniture making, vehicle
repair, maize flour production, dry cleaning, bread making, leather goods, knit wear, electrical
accessories, window casement manufacturing, castor oil production, tailoring, etc. To assist this
program, grants would be provided with Jua Kali Associations through MRTT&T. Special
attention is required by MRTT&T. DAT and the Jua Kali Associations to focus on and encoura2e
women to use the Jua Kali facilities, given their mobility and financial constraints. and the need to
balance their domestic and income onportunities. Data collection and monitoring on tender
access to sites, and to technology grants and trainip2 (in manufacturina rather than trade and
services), which are also to be involved witb the Jua Kali Association, will therefore be essential.
10.   Documentation to be Prepared and Tendering Procedures: Designs, documentation and
bidding documents for the basic infrastructure would be undertaken by a consortium of local
engineers/architects (selected under IDA procurement procedures) and include the following:
roads and paved areas, lighting and power supply, water reticulation, storm water disposal,
fencing, refuse disposal facilities, toilet/sanitary blocks, office for the Jua Kali Association and a
store for building materials, which after completion of the operator sheds, be converted to an
exhibition shed or technology center. The infrastructure would be tendered under LCB
procedures because of its small value and as it is unlikely these contracts would go to foreign
contractors due to their small size and the 7 1/2% preference to local contractors if ICB
procedures were used. The consultant would also design some sample operator sheds, in
consultation with Jua Kali operators and the Association, for the operators and small contractors
where operators are unable to construct their own facilities. Standard layout drawings would
consider different type layouts, based on the simplest construction techniques, for each possible
operation to be considered. In the case of operators who have already received title to land and
have built sheds and are operating a business and there is no infrastructure, operators need to be
advised that they will be required to pay additional charges for the infrastructure when this has
been completed.
11.   Construction of Sheds: Some building materials are to be supplied through the credit,
obtained under ICB procedures, and distributed to the sites by the consultant consortium group.
These would be purchased by the better established operators who would be charged at a nominal
rate over period of time. Operators will essentially be responsible for constructing their own
structures, on a force account basis, however, assistance in construction and some basic training
in building techniques will be given, free of charge, through the Jua Kali Association, a clerk of
works and with possible support from the local Ministry of Public Works. The consultant would
tender sheds to local contractors, on behalf of those operators, who are not established and are
unable to effect the construction themselves.



95                         ANNEX 8
Page 4 of 11
12.   Construction Costs: Construction costs are based on up-dated contract prices from the
GOK/GTZ projects at Voi, Karatina, Kisi, Nakuru and Meru and are applicable at July 1, 1993.
Prices on each of these five contracts have escalated by approximately 80% since start-on-site date
April, 1992, and where all contracts will be complete by August, 1993. The anticipated final cost
of these five projects is infrastructure Kshs. 81 million and professional fees Kshs. 6 million.
Total cost Kshs. 87 million (US$1.3 million at Kshs. 65 per US$ exchange rate). Detailed costs
are as follows:

This Project:

Note: The final cost of infrastructure on the GOK/GTZ project considers increased prices
due to escalation and additional works since the April, 1992 start-on-site date to August, 1993
when all sites have been handed over to the Jua Kali Associations. Considering the past year and
current rates of inflation, it is envisaged that these prices will escalate further by approximately
50% to project start date July, 1994, project construction prices have therefore been adjusted
accordingly.
13.   Available Sites at Kisumu: The appraisal mission visited two sites at Kisumu which have
been proposed for improvement. These were:
(i) Kisumu Town: Area 3.5 hectares (8.5 acres). Operated by 2 Jua Kali Associations
who have amalgamated into the Kisumu Center Jua Kali Association which is run by a
management committee consisting of a Chairman, Vice Chairman, Secretary, Vice Secretary,
Organizing Secretary, Vice Organizing Secretary and 8 Committee members. The Association,
which has yet to be registered, includes 400-500 operators with only 10 women members. Main
operations carried out on site include motor vehicle repairs, spray painting, welding and
fabricating, waste paper re-cycling, metal work and electrical repairs. Land title was originally
with Kenya Railways, however, this has been in abeyance since 1987 and it was advised that thi.
had not been renewed and title had therefore reverted back to Government. The Jua Kali
Association needs to urgently acquire a letter of allotment to ensure proper title is obtained. The
-ite contains two sheds (ea( X 5X20 meters) and an office which have been constructed by
MRTT&T. The site has no sanitary facilities, no water services and minimal electrical provision,
however, main drains, eiectrical services and water are readily available off site (an existing
75mm diameter and 150mm diameter water main pass the boundary on Nyuki Road and Johanna
Ouku Road respectively; a 225mm diameter concrete sewer pipe; and, a three phase power line
adjacent to the site boundary). The JKA currently pay KShs. 19,600 in service charges and
license fee to the Kisumu City Council and members are charged KShs.370 per year which covers
these charges and the operational costs of the Association. Suggested plot requirements for a new
development would be: 25% = 10in X 16m; 45% = 6m X 10m; and, 30% = 6m X 6 m.
(ii) Kibuye Location at Kisumu: Area 3.1 hectares (7.6 acres), however only 2.5 hectares
available for development. Operated by the Kibuye Jua Kali Association, which is registered, and
with a similar committee as for Kisumu. Kisumu City Council have agreed to give the land to the
JKA and a letter to this effect with site plans needs to be lodged with MRTT&T to assist in the
obtainng of a letter of allotment. The Association currently has a total membership of 643 and

includes 161 men and 120 women members. 900 trainees are also attached. Each member pays
KShs. 120 per year with a joining fee of KShs. 150. The Citv Council collect KShs. 120 from each

Ground flooding evident at bottom end of site. Letter of allotment exists from the Department of

(ii) Kaa Chonjo 2: Area 0.96 hectares (2.4 acres). Centrally located with 48 possible plots

(iii) Miritini: Area 1.16 hectares (2.9 acres). Located four miles from Town center near
to Match Factory with 36 plots of varying size which have yet to be allocated. Site is clear with
no structures evident and essential services are available off site. Letter of allotment exists from
Department of Lands. Access to site from main road adequate. Infrastructure could be funded by

(iv) Chaani Open Market: Area 0.42 hectare (1 acre). Site located in the World Bank
financed Chaani site and service project and which was originally scheduled for one of two open
air markets in a heavily populated domestic area. The site, which could contain 67 sub-plots, has
remained unused for the past five years. The site has a perimeter wall and contains an ablution
block and a small office. Essential services exist and access is by tarmac road. The reasons for
this site remaining unused over the past five years will need to be assessed carefully and a firm
list of possible Jua Kali operators wishing to trade here would need to be established before IDA
could consider funding the infrastructure.
(v) Likoni: Area 2.72 hectares (6.7 acres). Site located off main south road from
Mombasa (2-3 miles) going towards Diane Beach. The site is well located in a growing
population area and currently contains a few minor structures within its overall area. The site
could contain 115 sub-plots of varying sizes and is readily accessible from the main tarmac road
adjoining it. Essential services are also available outside the site boundaries. A letter of
allotment exists from the Department of Lands. Infrastructure could be funded by IDA.

D. Financial Management
15.   Cost Recoverv: Rents to be Charged: The rents would be charged primarily on the basis
of the market rates for similar facilities in each town. There will not be a uniform national rate.
The rents for the work places under this project are likely to be higher than market rates since
additional facilities are provided as compared to the sites where they operate at present. This is
sensible considering many Jua Kali businesses are already paying rents at market rates. The rents
would be determined reflecting the costs of construction and land value, the provision of services
(electric, water, sanitation and refuse collection), and on-going maintenance costs. Rents would
be reviewed annually and indexed to a measure of inflation. In order to be able to attract
fiancing agencies and investors to the informal sector infiastructure investment, it will be
ensured that rents should yield an economic rate of return of 15 percent over 15 years (although
this may not attract private investors at this stage, it will provide an incentive for the investment
at a later stage). The Jua Kali Association would be entitled to terminate the lease if the tenants
fail to pay rents more than three months and/or other charges such as service charges, license
fees, statutory charges to the local authorities and the Ministry of Commerce.
16.   Cost Recovery: Use of Funds and Collateral for Loans: Payments and charges collected
would consider total cost recovery. Two project accounts would be kept where all receipts would
be split on a 15% and 85% basis. The 15% account covering costs of the maintenance of
infrastructure and services reticulation, whilst the second account would support expansion to
overall site activities, additional operating staff salaries, land acquisition for future expansion and
provision of credit facilities to those operators -equiring additional equipment and tools (at easy
terms and standard interest rates). Where operators hold the individual title to plots, it will be
possible for them to use this title as ^ollateral for borrowing funds from commercial houses.
Other operators, who lease land from the Jua Kali Association over ten years, will aot have this
resource, and will need to arrange a chattel mortgage with banks through their ownership of
equipment and tools which would be put up as collateral against a loan.
17.   Maintenance/Management and Development Accounts: The rents collected would be
deposited in two separate accounts. About 15 percent of the total monthly revenue would be
deposited in an operational account (Jua Kali Operational Fund) for maintenance and
management. This amount should be adjusted according to ages of the work places and local
conditions so that it may be sufficient to cover management, and proper maintenance and repairs.
The balance would be deposited in a development account (Jua Kali Infrastructure Fund). This
surplus capital in the Jua Kali Infrastructure Fund would be invested in short term and medium
term securities and would upon request be ploughed back into further development of the original
site, additional Jua Kali sites, or provision of credit to operators who require tools and equipment
and where loans would be provided at easy terms and standard interest rates. The Jua Kali
Infrastructure Fund would be managed by the Project Steering Committee and regularly inspected
by Finance and Accounts Department (FAD), MRfT&T. The two accounts, Jua Kali Operational
Fund and Jua Kali Infrastructure Fund would be audited annually by independent auditors.



98                          ANNEX S
Page 7 of 11
18.   Jua Kali Committee: The Jua Kali Committee (JKC), composed of representatives of
local Jua Kali Associations, and Federation of Jua Kali Associations, the private sector, IDA,
MRTT&T, Local Authorities, and other GOK line ministries. Inclusion of the local auth1ority
representatives would help identify the Jua Kali sites for future development. The JKC would be
chaired by the MRTT&T Permanent Secretary. The principal responsibilities of the JKC would
be to manage the Jua Kali Infrastructure Fund and to determine the list of the eligible businesses
for each Jua Kali si.e under the project.
19.   Letter of Allotment/Title Charges: To obtain a letter of allotment from the Commissioner
of Lands (COL) various charges are levied which include a stand premium (GOK premium rate of
current land value) which is a one-tim.- payment to the COL when land has been offered to a non-
government group or an individual. This charge has to be settled within 30 days after receirt of
the letter of allotment. The example below for Kaa Chonjo TI on Mombasa Island outlines other
charges which are levied. The stand premium in this case was much lower than the market rate:
e.g. Kshs. 68,000 versus a market value of Kshs. 21.0 million. Land rents are also levied by the
COL and are required to be settled yearly from the date of issuance of the letter of allotment.
These rents vary to location and are much higher in Mombasa than Kisumu. Land rates are also
required by the local government authority annmally after the letter of allotment is issued.
Repayment of the cost of infrastructure varies according to its actual cost and is split between
operator sites over period of time. Maintenance and lua Kali management charges are established
at 1-2% of the cost of infrastructure. (see attachment to this Annex)

E. Provgram Management
20.   Tmplementation and Mana;etent: MRTT&T/DAT/ATU would have the overall
responsibility for project implementation. This unit would be reinforced with additional staff,
supported through the credit and for the life of the project only, and include a
Coordinator/Economist, Financial Officer, Proumentfrtucture Specialist, Monitoring and
Evaluation Specialist, Training/Planning Specialist, Technology/Planning Specialist and a Staff
Development Specialist. DAT/ATU would be responsible for the contracting out and appointment
of consultant services to groups and individuals to address the Training Fund, Infrastrucure
Development, Technology Development, Monitoring and Evaluation and Staff Development.
Each contract/package would be bid under IDA procedures, however, where a foreign firm was
judged to be the lowest responsive bid, tbat firm would be expected to participate with a local



99                             ANNEX 8
Page 8 of 11
consultant partner, to build local consultant capacity. DAT/ATU would also act as MRTT&T's
direct link with the Jua Kali Federation, again to receive some support through the Credit, and the
Jua Kali Associations throughout lx>enya.
21.   Jua Kali Association: Committee and Additional Staffing: Jua Kali Associations are
controlled by a democratically elected committee which includes a Chairman and Vice Chairman;
Treasurer and Vice Treasurer; Secretary and Vice Secretary; Organization Secretary and 6-10
other committee members. Associations at the project sites in Mombasa and Kisumu would be
reinforced with additional staff who would be responsible for the distribution of building
materials, training in building techniques, constructien controls and advice generally. (See
Annex 4 for further detailed description of Jua Kali Federation and Associatior.s).
22.   Jua Kali Association: Function: Individual programs will be managed by the Jua Kali
Association organized at each site. This method will provide accountability of management and a
sense of ownership among the beneficaries through their active participation in the design,
elaboration, aid implementation of the project. The finctions of the Jua Kali Associations would
include: (a) collection of rents; (b) managing a Jua Kali Operational Account; (c) management and
maintenance of infrastructure; (d) maintining records of all lease holders; (e) maintaining
observance of lease conditions; (f) transfer of plots; and, (g) provision of construction training
and materials to operators, and supervision of individual constructions. The Association should
-xercise internal control to prevent speculation and illegal sale, subletting, or transfer of the work
places. Through its by-laws, the Association can guarantee that the withdrawing member will sell
or return the work places to the Jua Kalis only. The Jua Kali Association would be subject to
public scrutiny and audit, and report to MRTT&T. MRTT&T would assume the role to facilitate
and supervise the overall infastructure program.
23.   Support to the Jua Kali Association: Since the Jua KLli Associations at present do not
have all the skills required for the complex process of the infrastructure project, external support
is required. The Federation of Jua Kali Associations should assume a role as support
organizations which provide skills and resources with a policy framework with respect to land,
finance, and so forth. To strengthen the capacity of Jua Kali Associations and the Federation,
technical assistance through the appointment of a consortium of management and
architect/engineering consultant firm will be provided in the start-up phase.
24.   Training for the Jua Kali Association: The management of the Association is critical to
reaching the goals of the project. Good management applies equally to the Association and the
supporting organizations such as the MRTT&T. The project will provide management training
for representatives of the Jua Kali Associations and the Federation of the Jua Kali Associations.
In addition, individual members' participation is important in the management of the Association.
To enable the membership to participate, there needs to be a suitable structure but this should be
underpinned by the development of members' skills through trai-ung and education. The content
of training should cover many aspects of the operations of the Association with more general
courses for the ordinary membership and more intensive training for the elected leadership.
Human resources development should be built into the structure of the Association on a
continuing basis.
25. MIonitoring and Evaluation of Sites: The project includes funds for monitoring and
evaluating of all sites included in the Credit as well as other sites to be funded by other donors
which could be implemented differently from this Credit. The most appropriate method of



100                            ANNEX 8
Page 9 of 11
implementation and management for the establishment of a small scale enterprise can then be
determined for the future.
F. Criteria for Selecding Allottee's of Work Places
26.   Selection Criteria for Allottee's: The selection procedure to ensure proper and protected
ownership of title would be totally transparent where a selection conunittee (represented by
MRTT&T, the Local Authority, local Jua Kali Association, Jua Kali Federation and District
Development Committee) would short-list suitable operators based on the following criteria: i) be
a bona fide member of the local Jua Kali Association; ii) have a successful record in small
business operation; iii) has been in operation for at least two years; iv) is able to afford the
rent/charges to be levied; v) is in a trade/craft which has growth potential; vi) do not currently
own other commercial plots iD town; and vii) the plot to be acquired fits the type of business to
be operated from it. To avoid speculation by unscrupulous entrepreneurs purchasing one or more
plots and sub-letting to others at exorbitant rents, the selection committee will ensure that only the
most needy and deserving operators wil become participants to receive one plot only and that
reasonable and affordable rents/charges will be levied. However, if a recipient is unable to find
all the rent for his/her plot, he or she will report to the Jua Kali Association which would discuss
this and allow him/her to share the facility and rents with other artisans.
G. Allocation Procedures
27.   Applications; Applications would be invited for the work places under the project.
Extensive advertisements would be arranged through local publications, radio and respective Jua
Kali Associations. The information on the available facilities and services would be provided.
Accordingly, the application form would clearly state: (a) the number of work places available;
(b) the sizes of each work place, and available facilities and services ; (c) the tenure arrangement;
and (d) the monthly rent an other charges. Easy access to application forms would be ensured for
all Juan Kalis in the town. Each application form would charge a non-refundable KSh.50, which
would be deposited in the Juan Kali Operational Fund.
28.   The application form would request the following information:
-name and ID No. of the applicant
-type of Business
-number of years in operation in the town
-number of employees (i, any)
-estinated daily/weekly/monthly/ turnover
-rent paid at present
-details of trade licenses held with the local authority and the Ministry of Commerce
The detailed business plan should be attached to the application form. Juan Kali
Associations would help entrepreneurs prepare the business plans. Technical assistance will be
provided for Jua Kali Associations in the first stage.
29.   Ballotin,: it is anticipated that there will be more qualified applicants than work places
available. Therefore, the applicants would be balloted. The balloting should be carried out
following transparent and accountable procedures and be done publicly under the supervision of
the selection committee. It should be ensured that local politics would not disrupt the process.



101
ANNEX 8
Page lOof 11
The results would be posted in a public place and communicated to individual applicants. The
selected applicants would then be required to sign a contract within a period of 14 days from
notification of allotnent.

B. TYPICAL STED CONSTRUCTION COSTS
Utilizing actual final conti act cost information provided from the GOK/GTZ projects at
Voi, Karatina, Kisii, Nakuru and Meru and assuming the average shed to be 6mx3m in size
excluding a working yard of similar area (total area 6m:x6m), a cost per shed at July, 1993 was
Kshs. 98,837 (US$1,521) or Kshs. 5491 (US$85) per square meter. Applying a 50% price
escalation to July, 1994, the approximate date of effectiveness, the cost per shed would increase
to Kshs. 148,000 (US$2,277) at a square meter cost of Kshs. 8,237 (US$ 127).
Different structure of sheds will be required depending on the occupation of Jua Kalis.
For example, spray painting or auto vehicle repairs would need only roof without fixed walls,
while tailoring would require more fixed structure for security. It is assumed that there is an
inverse relationship between the size of shed and the extent of its fixed structure: i.e., the larger
the shed is, the less structure is required. The cost per shed is thus expected to be the same for
all three sizes, Kshs. 148,000 (US$2,277). Total costs for 500 sheds in the project would add up
to Kshs. 74 million (USS1.2 million).
C. OPERATING COSTS PER ANNUM AT EACH SITE
Assumed as follows:
Kshs
Rent, rates, road charges, etc. to municipality         20,000
Water for communal facilities                           30,000
Electricity for communal facilities                     50,000
Maintenance/Operating costs                             50,000
TOTAL                                            150,000
D. FINANCIAL SUSTAINABILITY
The rents for sheds would be determined based on the principle of the financial
sustainability of this component of the project, while there would be no charge for the basic
infrastructure provided. Assurming the average operator will purchase a 6mx6m site and shed at a
total cost of Kshs. 148,000, the rents per shed would be Kshs. 25,310 per annum to ensure that
rents yield an economic rate of return of 15 percent over 15 years (see para. 15 in this Annex).
This means that the monthly rent per shed is Kshs. 2,110, or Kshs. 59 per mordi per square
meter of the site. While there is no precise data available for the rents Jua Kalis pay for a shed in
Mombasa or Kisumu, the information on the current rents in five towns collected for the GTZ
project provides a good reference. Given the size of town and its economic activities, Nakuru is
considered to be comparable to Kisumu and Mombasa. In Nakuru Jua Kali operators pay
monthly rents ranging from Kshs. 1,300 to Kshs. 7,000 for similar facilities with secure lockable
premises made of permanent materials, including drainage, and electricity. Considering the
location of the project sites, an anticipated rent of Kshs. 2,110 is thought to be reasonable.
About 15 percent of the rents collected would be deposited in a Jua Kali Operational Fund
for maintenance and management of the site, while the balance would be deposited in a Jua Kali
Infrastructure Fund (para. 17 in this Annex). Assuming a 70% (230 plots) occupancy out of the
330 plots on each site location, the JKA annual receipts from operators would be Kshs. 5.8
million for the rent of the sheds. This means that about Kshs. 870,000 per annum would be
allowed for the operating costs presented above, plus salaries of staff in the JKA, and the
remaining Kshs. 5 million would be invested through the Jua Kali Infrastructure Fund. Separate
fmancial statements would be required for the two funds and they would be subject to external
audit.

REPUBLIC OF KENYA
MICRO-AND SMALL ENTERPRISE TRAINING AND TECHNOLOGY PROJECT
THE MICRO- AND SMALL ENTERPRISE TRAINING FUND
I. Background
1.    Lack of managerial, technical, and entrepreneurial skills and modem technology are invariably
cited as major constraints to the competitiveness and growth of informal sector enterprises. However,
skill upgrading and on-the-job training is not readily available and access to appropriate technology is
limited. The public training system is not flexible enough to provide skill upgrading for Jua Kali
entrepreneurs and operators, although there are technical training institutes that could provide such
training if assisted in the development of courses. The same can be said about private training providers,
including enterprises.
2.    As a whole, the current training system is ineffective and financially unsustainable in that: (a)
training provisions are seldom matched to demand, (b) consumers have little or no choice in the type of
training they want, (cj there is no evidence that formal training leads to jobs or generates income, and
(d) private sector participation is low. There is a need for more relevant training such as employer-based
training which would also facilitate moving skill upgrading closer to productivity and employment.
3.    The Project Training Fund would become part of a national training strategy. It would develop
financing mechanisms (i.e., a Jua Kali training fund) as well as experience and lessons to be incorporated
in the modernization of the Industrial Training Levy scheme and thus enable project sustainability. This
process is likely to involve consolidation and privatization of training, facilitating a larger role for the
private sector and enterprises in skills training, especially regarding training facilities and cost sharing,
and improving institutional mechanisms linking the Government, industry and workers.
H. Objectives
4.    The Training Fund will help establish a financing system to accomplish the following three
objectives: (a) provide relevant and equitable skill upgrading programs to micro- and snall enterprises,
promoting equal access of women to the informal manufactring sector; (b) facilitate more effective
utilization of existing services and programs offered by public and private training institutions, and (c)
develop enterprise-based training and thereby enhance cost-sharing for the different training and
technology courses, in order to make the system more relevant and financially sustainable.
5.    The Training Fund will serve as a mechanism for channeling public resources on a competitive
basis to sub-projects at: (a) link both technical and managerial skill upgrading and access to information
and new/appropriate technology, and (b) encourage enterprise-based skll upgrading. By matching
informal bector clients with specialized training institutions, the Fund can provide an incentive for
developing private and public technical and managerial skldls training and technological support services,
including enterprise-based slkll upgrading.
6.    By establishing two related approaches to funding training through a voucher and contact
scheme, the Fund addresses specific financial and quality issues related to reorienting the training system



106
ANNEX 9
Page 2 of 12
to a demand-driven system. The voucher program would enable Jua Kalis to purchase the training they
want from approved training providers. The contract scheme would enable public and private institutions,
including enterprises, to provide training to informal sector clients on a competitive basis. A guide to
drft Government decision establishing the Project Trining Fund is attached to this Annex.
III. Fund Management
7.    While the Fund would be governed by a Project Steering Committee, the main agency to
administer the Fund and its programs will be the Training and Gender Unit (TGU) at MRTT&T/DAT
in conjunction with the Jua Kali Federation and local Associations. The TGU's principal responsibility
will be to make decisions regarding sub-project funding up to US$10,000. The sub-projects will be
executed by public or private institutions as well as enterprises which must compete for Fund resources
under pre-defined qualification and selection criteria outlined below. The project will provide technical
assistance to establish the Project Training Fund based on the general principles set forth in this Annex.
In particular allocation/procurement criteria would be clearly defined, including procedures for recovering
ineligible expenses, so as to allow for reallocation of funds among components from time to time
depending on actual performance and actual verifiable expenses.
8.    The DAT/TGU will report to the Project Steering Committee (PSC), comprising representatives
of MRTT&T and other GOK line ministries, along with Jua Kali Federation/Association and IDA
representatives. The PSC will be chaired by the MRTT&T Permanent Secretary. The PSC will serve
as a convening body for the parties involved in the Project, develop skill training policies, and stipulate
criteria for program promotion. The PSC will set annual budgets and review project proposals in excess
of US$10,000.
9.    The DAT/TGU will be responsible for the day-to-day administration of Project Fund activities.
This will involve reviewing and processing sub-project proposals on awarding funds (contracts, vouchers
and technology study visits) in consultation with the PSC.  The DAT/TGU  and Jua Kali
Federation/Associations which represent Jua Kali operators' interests and act as primary vehicles for
consultation and information exchange, will be responsible for organizing and reaching informal sector
entrepreneurs and artisans.
IV. Program
A. The Voucher Progam
a. Desciption
10.   Under the Project, a competitive voucher program aims to distribute up to 30,000 vouchers,
on average 6,000 per year, after the program has been gradually phased in to allow for learning
opportunities. The program has the following targets: a total of 10,000 vouchers at a unit cost of US$150
for management training and 20,000 vouchers for technical skill upgrading at a unit cost of US$200,
including trade testing II or I. A typical skill upgrading course would last about 2 to 6 weeks (including
enterprise-based, evening, onsite and residential courses). Vouchers could be used for public and private
sector instituions and enterprises that provide access to skill upgrading and technology development to
the micro- and small enterprise sector. Since vouchers give clients the purchasing power to select among
private or public institutons of their choice, this financing approach (pricing of the end product) is



107
ANNEX 9
Page 3 of 12
particularly useful to help develop a market for training and thus prevent oversupply of any one type of
training and control costs.
11.   The voucher program would make provision for increasing women's representation in the
lucrative manufacturing sector. Particular attention would be paid to women's access to skills training
and technology suitable for upgrading their enterprises or for bringing them into the sector. To this end,
women would benefit from up to 50% basic technical skill training. Several vouchers would be awarded
to one individual to cover longer-termn enterprise-based attachments (see sections b. and c. below). To
be gender responsive, training sub-components would be flexible, yet targeted. While it may be easy to
award up to 50% of a given number of vouchers to women at the lower skill level, it may be difficult
to reach more than 10% women at the middle or upper skill levels.
12.   As a whole, the voucher program would facilitate skill upgrading in areas such as technical skills
and business management skills (accounting, computer applications, advisory services, elementary sales
techniques and product handling, product design and diversification, product marketing, standards
application and adaptation, sub-contracting as well as choice and use of appropriate technologies).
Eliibili criteria in the vouchers program would include the entrepreneur's and employee's background
(education/training and work experience), the growth potential of the particular business/trade, and gender
sensitivity. Priority would be given to training master craftsmen who could then improve the informal
apprenticeship system and enterprise-based training.
b. Eligibility and Award Criteria
13.   Jua Kali Associations in consultation with PTTO, YTO and other relevant judges (i.e., technical
assistance provided under the project) will screen potential enterprises and trainees to benefit from the
voucher program in order to ensure that: (a) they are suitable for skill upgrading, especially regarding
their intentions and backgrounds; and (b) they are likely to benefit from it. To this end, the Jua Kali
Associations would use the information provided on the application for membership of enterprises and
hold regular consultative meetings. Registration forms for the voucher program would be distributed free
of charge by the TGU secretariat and would be obtained at the regional association offices or detached
from official advertisements in national newspapers. The local Jua Kali Association would apply for the
total number of vouchers needed on a competitive basis and coordinate their distribution.
Enterprises /lEneeneurs eligible for the vouchers would have to meet the following
requirements:
- fill in a registration form for voucher program, which is distributed by the TGU
- be micro- or small enterprise registered with MRTT&T (1 to 49 employees)
- have a specific product line with growth potential
- have been in the same business for 2 to 3 years
- agree to pay opportunty costs.



108
ANNEX 9
Page 4 of 12
Trainees/Employees eligible  or the vouchers would have to  meet the  following
requirements:
- fill in a registration form for voucher program, which is distributed by the TGU
- present trade test (III) or equivalent experience in trade
- have been employed for 2 to 3 years in the same trade
- have been on the payroll for six months before and remain thereon after training
provided that in the case of women, new entrants would be allowed direct entry into the training
program.
As a strategy to increase equity and incendves to improve entrepreneurs' and employees'
responsiveness and performance, additional vouchers may be issued to beneficiaries in cases where: a)
the trainee passes a grade test (II) and wishes to further upgrade his/her skills to pass trade test I (highest
grade); or b) the trainee wants to enter the sector through longer-term enterprise-based attachments, i.e.
women entrepreneurs.
Jua Kali Associations which meet the following criteria will be qualified to implement the
voucher program:
- they must have been registered with the MRTT&T for at least one year
- other criteria based on the number of registered members (micro- and small enterprises) and
their cost sharing ability and agreement.
c. Jmplementatlon/Adm    atlon Process
The roles and responsibilities of the MRTT&T and the Jua Kali Federation/Associations involved
in program coordination/management are as follows:
MRTT&T/DAT/TGU
The Training Unit (TGU), in consultation with the Project Steering Committee, will:
- be responsible for day-to-day administration
- develop a market for skills training responding to micro- and small enterprise training and
technology needs
- advise technical and managerial training providers in the preparation of project proposals
- review and process proposals on the basis( dentified informal sector training/technology needs
requirements (see Annex 11)



109
ANNEX 9
Page 5 of 12
- prepare terms of reference and contracts required for executing projects
- provide Jua Kali associations or equivalent with guidelines and schedules describing program
and application procedures
- ensure that sub-project applications be submitted conform to eligibility criteria
- ensure that vouchers be designed, printed and distributed
Jua Kali Associations
The local Jua Kali Association with assistance from the Federation would be responsible for:
- sensitizing personnel and members, as well as women's organizations to mobilize
female membership, about the Project and informing them about the voucher program
(i.e., throug: Jua Kali magazine and marketing exhibitions and other fora)
- monitoring training and technology needs in the sector (i.e., through membership application
and DYTO and VSO officers -- see Annex 11)
- selection of enterprises/trainees and matchmaking through training officers/advisers and training
counseling (i.e., establish information network)
- applying periodically for the total number of vouchers allocated to Jua Kalis
- signing an agreement with the MRTT&T for the voucher program administration and monitoring
of the program at the local level
- defining additional criteria for selecting trainees if the demand for vouchers surpasses
- establishing national data base on enterprise-based training opportunities (involve District
chainyan and Provincial representatives -- see Annex 11)
d. Cost-sharing/Financing
14.   Under the voucher progratn, the beneficiaries will share the cost in terms of opportunity costs
Incurred by the training (i.e., lost income, transport and supplies). Although the Training Fund will
finance ninety percent of the voucher and remaining ten percent by the trainees in the initial stage, Jua
Kali Associations and/or individual artisans will be eventually expected to contribute to the full cost of
the training a t a later stage. Once the training schemes have proven themselves, flexible but competitive
fee paying agreements will be worked out between the Jua Kali Associations and the training institutions
(in consultation with PTTOs/YTOs). It also should be noted that training modalities will be flexible (i.e.,
easy access through outreach programs), in order to minimize opportunity costs. Training services will
be selected by the beneficiaries themselves.
15.   Administrative costs for MRTT&T would be reflected in the Training Unit's budget. According
to the agreement signed between the MRTT&T and the Jua Kali Association, the services provided by



110
ANNEX 9
Page 6 of 12
the Jua Kali Federation/Association would be free of charge.
16.   Procedure for payment of vouchers involves the following general steps:  First, the
MRTr&T/DAT would submit to the MRTT&T/Finance and Accounts Department (FAD) voucher
programs for funding up to US$3,000 to be paid out of the Project Account. Second, the FAD would
deliver the vouchers to the eligible Jua Kali Associations. Trainees would receive the vouchers from the
Association and they would select training programs. In the event the trainee gets more than one
voucher, the trainee is able to transfer to other institutions. Training vouchers can be redeemed for cash
at the FAD by the approved training providers.
e. Audit/Monitoring
The DAT and the Jua Kali Federation/Associations involved in program implementation will have
the main responsibility for monitoring the voucher program.
MRTT&T will:
- ensure that the voucher program be effectively managed
- ensure that programs be monitored and supervised (see Annexes 17, 18, 19)
- ensure that sub-projects are executed in a timely manner and that the necessary financial
disbursements are similarly timely
- ensure reallocation of funds if necessary and reinforce procedures for recovering ineligible
expenses
- maintain and update directories of public and private training providers annually
Jua Kali Federation/Associations will:
- monitor the voucher program and periodically issue information reports to MRTT&T/DAT
- maintain and update directories of enterprise-based training opportunities annually
B. The Traning Contract Scheme
a. Description
17.   T}e contract scheme aims to award up to 1,500 training contracts for various courses and services
on a competitive basis. An average of 300 sub-projects are expected to be submitted to the Fund
anmually, ranging from enterprise-based skill upgrading to advanced tailor-made courses. Group-based
training would comprise 10-15 trainees each for technical training and 15-25 trainees each for
management training. A total of 30,000 entrepreneurs and employees are expected to benefit from
contract training.



^                 ~~~~~~111
ANNEX 9
Page 7 of 12
18.   Two broad types of sub-projects have been identified for Training Fund financing: (a) enterprise-
based training (up to 50 percent of total contracts) and (b) residential and on-site skill upgrading in
technical and managerial subjects, including technical assistance for entrepreneurship development
(graduation) of small enterprises (up to 60 percent of total contracts). Employers who provide on-site
skill upgrading can receive reimbursement of up to 100 percent (within approved ceilings) for upgrading
training equipment related to skills upgrading and technology development. Training contracts can
include financing of: training of trainers, training-related equipment and instructional materials in basic,
intermediate and advanced courses in the main crafts/trades.
b. Eligibility and Award Criteria
19.   To ensure demand responsiveness, providers will be required to submit proposals based on
identified training and technology needs. The institution's capacity to deliver proposed services and
maintain auditable accounts should be clearly evident. Since group training is generally more cost-
effective than individualized training, participating institutions will be expected to prepare group training
outlines, especially in management courses, according to the guidelines to be prepared and distributed
by the Training Unit. Training methods should be suitable to an adult population. Institutions should
be willing to establish links with Jua Kali Associations and offer acceptable, affordable and equitable skdll
improvement courses to those Jua Kalis nearest the institutions.
The criteria for participation in the training contract scheme by public and private institutions
would be as follows:
- they must provide complete courses (one of the outcomes is a product)
- they must have professional instructors (i.e., master craftsman)
- they must present acceptable trade test pass rate for trainees where applicable
- they must meet minimum facility requirements determined by MRTT&T standards
- they must provide supervision by training officers
- they must have technical capacity, equipment and relevant experience in providing training to
the sector.
In addition, training proposals, submitted by training institutions and enterprises must satisfy the
following criteria:
- they must be responsive to training and technology needs assessment
- they must use existing training capacity (e.g., ITCs)
- they must provide links both to skill upgrading and access to information and new/appropriate
technology
- they must provide a measure of cost recovery (e.g., infrastructure, equipment and fees)



112
ANNEX 9
Page 8 of 12
- they must maintain auditible accounts
- they must involve local employers in the training process
- the proposed training must be accessible to micro and small enterprises, especially owned by
women.
20.    Other specific criteria will be prepared by the Training and Gender Unit (TGU), DAT on a
regular basis. Institutions and enterprises selected for the contract program will be required to participate
in regular evaluations (studies and sample surveys) measuring the quality of training provided. Once the
monitoring and evaluation system is in place, improvement in quality indicators will be considered a
conditior for disbursement by the Bank (See also Attachment L for Project impact evaluation).
c. Implementation/Administration Process
21.   Once the project is announced, public and private training institutions and private enterprises will
be invited to submit sub-project proposals (including time frame, content, methods, cost and expected
outcome of the skill upgrading) to the TGU. Proposals for providing technical and managerial training,
as well as technological support services, will be reviewed and processed by the TGU in consultation with
the Project Steering Committee (PSC) on the basis of the established criteria as above. In principle,
training providers will be expected to develop sub-project proposals in consultation with the TGU and
Jua Kali Federation/Associations.
The selected training providers should present the TGU with the following information:
- details of enrollment capacity (present and projected)
- details of current training capacity (classrooms and other facilities, presence of trainers and
training materials)
- details of operating license and insurance
- details of training action plan and schedules
- details of course fee, monthly fee, etc. as listed in directory
22.   The TGU will also maintain directories of public and private training providers, including
enterprises, act as a match-making broker and advise approved technical training organizations and
enterprises in the preparation of project proposals and, where necessary, advise in their initial execution.
It will prepare terms of reference and contracts required for sub-project execution and ensure that sub-
project applications submitted to the TGU meet allocation criteria, such as training and technology needs
identified by the appropriate unit to be established at MRTT&T/PDU (see Annex 11). Moreover, to
prevent financing of productive work that would have taken place in any event, enterprise-based training
criteria will be the same as above and be closely monitored.



113
ANNEX 9
Page 9 of 12
d. Cost-sharing/Financing
23.   As a partial cost recovery strategy, beneficiaries are expected to pay minimal training fees, similar
to those currently charged by the ITCs for Jua Kali artisans. Once the training schemes have proven
themselves, flexible but competitive fee paying arrangements could be worked out between the Jua Kali
Associations and the training institutions (in consultation with PTTOstYTOs). The underlying assumption
of this approach is that demanding fees (even non-economic ones) for services provides an indication that
the services are of value. Therefore, it can be expected that training fees will adjust to demand if
information about costs and training outcomes is available to clients. In this way, trainir'g institutions
can be held accountable for price and quality of training available in the market place.
24.   Contracts will be awarded on the basis of the number of trainees to be trained and active
recruitment of women. They will be limited to maximum amounts of money (i.e., US$3,600 average
amount per contract/course). However, cumulative financing for any given enterprise or institution will
be determined by market forces and quality indicators, given the competitive basis of the skill upgrading
schemes.
25.   To provide incentives for public and private institutions, such as the ITCs and private enterprises,
to participate in the program, they should have operational autonomy. This would especially require that
the ITCs have the authority to retain funds generated through skill upgrading courses and other income
generating activities for their institutional development.
26.   Procedure for payment of contracts would involve two basic steps: First, the MRTT&T/DAT
would submit to the MRTT&T Finance and Accounts Department (FAD) sub-projects for funding up to
US$10,000 to be paid out of the Project Account. Second, the FAD would reimburse training providers
for services delivered.
e. Audit/Monitoring
The MRTT&T/DAT Training Unit will have the main responsibility for monitoring the contract
scheme in consultation with the Project Steering Committee.
MRTT&TtDAT/Training Unit will:
- ensure that the contract scheme be effectively managed
- ensure that programs be monitored
- ensure sub-projects are executed in a timely manner and that the necessary financial
disbursements are similarly timely
- ensure reallocation of funds if necessary and reinforce procedures for recovering ineligible
expenses



114             ANNr-: 9
Page 10 of 12
C. Technology Study Visits
a. Descrir n
27.   The Project would sponsor about 200 techmology study visits for selected innovator/entrepreneurs
to East and South Asia and Africa. These visits would be organized for promising Jua Kali manufacturers
by product sub-sector and last up to 30 days. The visits could also include short attachments with foreign
enterprises. A panel of judges (including providers of snall enterprise programs would be selected to
identify the potential beneficiaries during market exhibitions or training. The panel would formalize the
nominations, including suitable places of visits or attachments.
b. Eligibility Criteria
The eligibility and award criteria of innovators/entrepreneurs eligible for the technology study
visits would be as follows:
- beneficiaries must have been nominated by the selection panel
- they must be promising innovators/entrepreneurs in a sub-sector
- they must have demonstrated experience with products and technologies having regard to
originality and quality of products, potential for commercialization and cost-effectiveness in
production methodologies
- they must have demonstrated improvements in productivity, e.g., job creation and profit
- they must have a strategy for product development and marketing
- they must have a business plan for enterprise development.
C. Implementation/Administaton Process
This program would be contracted out through the Center for Research and Technology (CRT)
at MRTT&T/DAT to machmaker/brokers utilizing ICB. It would be closely monitored to ensure that
the allowance is utilized for the intended purpose.
d. Cost-sharing/Fiancing
28.   The beneficiaries would share the costs in terms of oppotunity costs incurred during the training
(e.g., lost income, transport, registration fees, etc.). !7nancing of technology study visits would include
transportation costs, per diem, and related program operating costs. The project would also provide a
technology procurement allowance of up to $300 per participant to purchase a new piece of
equipment/technology for utilization in Kenya, while the cost exceeding this amount would be paid by
the participant. There would be no import tax duties on this equipment up to Ksh 20 million in value.
The participants would be required to submit reports of the study visit upon the completion of the their
visits and to attend technology and marketing exhibitions at least once to share their experiences. They
also may be required to participate in the training activities from tim t. time. The program would be
closely monitored so as to allow for reallocation of funds depending on actual performance and actual
verifiable expenses.

days of group-based training for one person. A voucher worth $200 might cover 10 full days of skdll
upgrading for one person.

REPUBLIC OF KENYA
MICRO-AND SMALL ENTERPRISE TRAINING AND TECHNOLOGY PROJECT
APPLIED TECHNOLOGY RESEARCH GRANTS PROGRAM
I. Purposes
1.    The purposes of the program are to: (1) stimulate applied technology research and innovation;
(2) encourage the participation of entrepreneurs in technological innovation; and (3) increase private
sector support for the connercialization of indigenous production technologies.
II. Description of Competitive Grants Program
2.    The Grant program consists of the following three (3) stages:
Stage 1.:    The objective is to establish the technical merit and feasibility of the proposed applied
research and to qualify the grantee for stage 2 funding. The expected output is a
comprehensive Feasibility Study Report. The grants are for a maximum of $3,000
with a performance period of from 6 to 9 months. The Project has allocated funds to
support at least 50 grant awards.
Stage 2.:    The objective is to continue the development efforts of Stage 1 with the aim of
developing an innovation which is expected to be commercialized in Stage 3. The
expected output(s) are a prototype and/or a patent given by the Kenya Industrial
Property Office (KIPO) for the innovation. The grant also has provisions to support
the preparation of a Commercialization Plan for the prototype or patent. The grants
are for a maximum of $10,000 with a performance period not to exceed 24 months.
The development of the prototype could be coordinated with the Kenya Industrial
Research and Develonment Institute (KIRDI) an agency under the MRTT&T with
staff and facilities specifically geared for prototype development. The Project has
allocations for at least 25 Stage 2 grant awards. Products or processes that are ready
for prototype development or patent registration may be eligible for Stage 2 funding if
the proponents satisfy the requirement of submission of Feasibility Study Report.
Stage 3:     The objective is to commercialize the results of Stage 2 developments involving the
business sector and utilizing private funds. No grant funds are available for this
stage.
III. Eligibility Criteria
3.    The following are eligible for the Grants Program: (1) Jua Kali innovators; (2) Research and
technology development institutions, public or private; and (3) Individuals and private business firms.
Individuals, firms and R&D institutions must have linkages with the Jua Kali sector in order to
qualify.



ANNEX 10
118                      Page 2 of 4
IV. Preparation of Stage 1 Proposal
4.    The innovation will be judged primarily on the quality of the proposal. Stage 1 proposals are
limited to 25 pages including all text, figures, etc. The content will include a description of the
innovation, how it relates to the Jua Kali sector, the technical background of the proponent and the
personnel involved in the proposed work, and the action plan for conducting the applied research.
5.    The proposals should be submitted to the Directorate of Research and Development (DRD) of
the MRTT&T (Attn: Applied Technology Research Grants Program). The Proposal mu:st be received
by the DRD before the deadline specified in the Notices to be publishet'd about the Grants Program.
6.    Proponents are eligible for only one Stage 1 Grant award for a particular innovation. If they
have more than one innovation, they are eligible for consideration for a grant for each different
innovation proposed.
V. Awards Criteria
7.    Grants will be awarded by the Permanent Secretary upon the recommendation of an Applied
Research Grants Awards Committee (the Committee) on the basis of the following criteria (with
corresponding weights):
a.    Technological quality, innovativeness and originality  40%
b.    Commercial significance of the product or process
(market potential)                                  20%
C.    Workplan                                             20%
d.    Qualifications, facilities & other resources of
proponent                                            20%
100%
VI. Awards Committee
8.    The DRD will organize the Committee to evaluate proposals and award grants to outstanding
technological innovations. The Conmmittee will be composed of the following:
a.    National Council for Science and Technology Representative - Chairman.
b.    Director of Research Development - Secretary
c.    Director of Applied Technology - Member
d.    Business Sector Representative - Member
e.    Jua Kali Federation Representative - Member
f.    Relevant experts as technical consultants to the Committee.



119
ANNEX 10
Page 3 of 4
9.    The Directorate of Research Development (DRD) will provide the technical secretariat and the
administrative support to the Awards Committee with the Director of Research Development acting as
Secretary of the Committee. The Director of Research Development will identify and recommend to
the Awards Committee relevant experts that can help the Committee make competent evaluation of
proposals.
10.   The Awards Committee will submit to the Permanent Secretary (PS), MRTT&T its
recommendation with regards to the winning technological innovations and the corresponding grant
amounts. The Permanent Secretary will make the final decision and announcement of the Grant
Awards.
VII. Awarding Dates
11.   The Awards Committee will accept and evaluate Applied Research Grant proposals two times
a year, e.g., March 15 and September 15 of every year. Announcement of winners will be made
within two (2) months of the closing dates.
VII. Feasibiity Study Report
12.   The Feasibility Study Report is the main output of Stage 1 and is the major requirement for
Stage 2 funding. The Feasibility Study Report is expected to cover the following major aspects of the
technological innovation: (1) role of the product (or process) in the particular industry; (2) market
survey and demand estimate; (3) technical feasibility; (4) cost-benefit analysis; (5) implementation
plan; and (6) budget proposal.
13.   In the preparation of the Feasibility Study Report, the proponent may wish to avail of the
services of the faculty and staff of Universities, National Polytechnics, Small Business Centers and
even consultants from business, industry or non-governental organization.
IX. Counterpart Funding
14.   Grant applicants are required to provide counterpart funding to the Applied Research Grants
equivalent to at least fifty percent (50%) of total grant amount. The counterpart funding may be a
cash outlay or an imputed cost consisting of existing personnel, equipment, buildings and other
facilities.
X. Targets and Budgets
15.   The attached Tables show the target minimum number of grants and maximum budget over
the 6-year life of the projet.

REPUBLIC OF KENYA
MICRO-AND SMALL ENTERPRISE TRAINING AND TECHNOLOGY PROJECT
ASSESSING TRAINING CAPACITY, SKILL AND
RELATED TECHNOLOGY NEEDS
I. Background
1.    Needs assessment capacity is central to establishing an effective and relevant training system.
To maintain a responsive system, information is required not only on the types of training offered in the
various institutions, but also on the demand for such training and skill upgrading. To obtain a cost
effective and sustainable system, it is crucial that existing training capacity, especially in public
institutions, be used fully and the performance and quality of training institutions and programs be closely
monitored. To make the system more effective, the design of skill upgrading programs must be both
market-driven and skills-driven (i.e., linked to the development and maintenance of standards of
performance in skills training as well as associated examinations and tests).
2.    The Ministry of Labor, through the National Employment Bureau, has been involved in some
labor market monitoring and has been attempting to run what could be called an employment service.
It comprises employment promotion and planning as well as guidance counselling for those who either
work or are seeking work. However, these services do not reach informal sector workers and they are
limited by a lack of data about the trained manpower actually supplied to the labor market. There is no
relevant information about vacancies (required by the Employment Service Rules of 1977), which would
provide a link between job seekers and employers, a situation which the ILO is helping to rectify.
Comprehensive data about trained labor, both within and outside the country, are needed to properly
monitor (a) the quality and quantity of training supply and outcomes, as well as (b) skill and technology
needs at various levels and (c) to develop training policies.
U1. Objectives
3.    Establishing a skill and technology monitoring and needs assessment function at the
MRTT&T/PDU will make the training system more responsive to skill and technology needs of the labor
market, including micro- and small enterprises. Such a system would be designed to provide ongoing
information on the training supply and the skill and teclmology needs of the labor market. Such
information will be disseminated through various media (publications, directories, exhibitions, etc.) in
order to inform training providers and beneficiaries about existing and required skill upgrading/training
programs and related support services. Where possible, the Monitoring and Evaluation Unit will rely
on existing sources of information (i.e., at the Ministry of Labor).
4.    In cases where no existing data sources are available this Unit will facilitate research and
evaluation studies. Objectives would include to: (1) determine technology levels within th;; sector and
technical problems hampering technological growth; (2) procure appropriate technological option: to these
identified technical problems; (3) carry out technical research in order to obtain relevant technology
packages for dissemination within the sector; or (4) evaluate the quality of training programs and trade
tests in collaboration with the Inspectorate, the DIT and employers through the National Industrial
Training Council (NITC).



122
ANNEX 11
Page 2 of 4
5.    The establishment of these key planning functions will strengthen the Ministry's capacity to
implement Government policy to respond to the skill and technology needs of productive sectors,
particularly the informal sector. The monitoring and evaluation system will provide guidance and criteria
for funding specific training and technology interventions. In the long term, with the cooperation of the
NITC and the National Jua Kali Federation/Associations, the MRTT&T will develop longer term training
strategies for the productive sectors on the basis of specific studies (including the assessment of the
Industrial Training Levy) as well as the country's economic development strategy. The following are
guidelines for designing and implementing a monitoring and evaluation capacity at MRTT&T.
IH. Monitoring and Evaluation
A. Assessig Training Capacity
6.    Facilitating matchmaking between training supply and informal sector skill upgrading needs will
be done through systematic monitoring and periodic evaluadton of training programs and providers. Such
information will be gathered and disseminated through various channels such as studies, surveys,
application forms, the Jua Kali magazine, and directories. They will be updated in the light of new
information.
Directories would provide simple comprehensive and up-to-date monitoring and evaluation of
training provided and available including:
a.    a directory of traing lnstitutions updated anually (public and private)
- mformation on relevant experience in the sector and operatng license
- data on skill upgrading courses and counseling (support services) provided
- data on scheduled programs and fees (i.e., training plan)
- records of trainers, particularly entrepreneurs and master craftsmen, who have been trained to
train others
- data on technical capacity equipment
b.    a directory of enterpise-based   aing opportuni es updated annually
- information on business details and relevant experience
- data on capacity (i.e., facilities, presence of in-plant instructors and training equipment)
- information on authorization to provide skill upgrading in a particular trade(s)
- information on skill training and attachments (including information on insurance)



123                         ANNEX 11
Page 3 of 4
7.    The design of new skill and production technology upgrading courses, as well as the development
of trade tests (III to 1) will be based both on: (1) an evaluation of the supply and outcomes of training
and (2) changing informal sector market demands and training needs. Policy research and surveys will
provide the following information:
c.    evaluation reports
- assessment and improvement of the quality of skill upgrading programs
- assessment and up-dating of trade tests linking skill upgrading and technology development
- survey data on training outcomes in enterprises (i.e., a welding product)
B. Assessing SkIll Upgading Needs
8.    Skill upgrading needs can be identified through various channels:  Jua Kali Association
membership applications, follow-up of market exhibitions, and training programs. Many Jua Kalis are
already among those registered clients of small enterprse programs such as KEE/ISP, K-REP, IYB, KIM
etc. as well as MRTT&T. The computeization of the trade testing system at MRTT&T/DIT and its bio-
data information on trainees will also help to gauge skill training provided and required.
Available information on skill upgrading needs can be disseminated through:
- a directory of Jua Kali associations which are interested in skill and management training for
their members
- MRTI&T/Jua Kali Federation/Associations' mobilization and outreach efforts
- sensitizing Jua Kalis themselves about available skldl upgrading opporanities
C. Assssing Production Technology and Requirments
9.    The determination of production technology capacity requirements will be mainly based on: (1)
research into the changing informal sector market demands and (2) regular follow-up assessments of the
market exhibitions and trade fairs (i.e., the quality of products and production methods and Jua Kali
products/services for export and sub-contracting promotion), as well as membership applications
indicating technology requirements. Such data will also be fed into the information clearing house, trade
exhibitions and technology study tours.
10.   For instance, survey research will focus on identification of all exportable products made by the
Jua Kali sector in the country and technical capacity and constraints affecting the quantity and quality of
production and efficiency of manufacturing productivity in the informal sector.
11.   Surveys of Jua Kali products and services for export and sub-contracting promotion would
also identify the appropriate operators to venture into the export market and the products/services that
could be used in sub-contracting exchange with other firms. The information will be particularly useful
to the National Federation of Jua Kali Associations, the Kenya External Trade Authority (KETA), the



124
ANNEX 11
Page 4 of 4
Ministry of Conmmerce and Industry and the Kenya sub-contracting program exchange. Surveys wo'ild
on a regular basis:
- identify those Jua Kali products/services that can be exported or used in sub-contracting
exchange program and make an invetory of the same on a computer data base as well as in
a catalogue to be updated regularly
- identify the obstacles faced by the Jua Kal 'perators that hinder the export or sub-contracting
of their products/services
- review the current sources of raw materials, tools and equipment in regard to price and quality,
and make appropriate recommendations
- review the products made in regard to quality and recommend appropriate training and
technology where required
- review and make recommendatons on design, packaging, pricing and promotion of the
products/services
- examine and recommend appropriate solutions to the current lack of market information
- identify Jua Kali artisans who are sub-contracted by other firms
12.   Other policy rdated research would focus on factors affecting technology choice, such as:
- the needs and priorities of entrepreneurs
- entrepreneurs' access to tools, skills, equipment maintenance and repair facilities, power
supply, training facilities and information on products, processes and techniques
- access to other resources such as cash, raw materials and markets
- sources of technology innovation and dissenination
- financial and technical resources needed to withstand the risks of new product development
- the lack of technical expertise needed for transfer of technologies
- business risks associated with new products
- linkages between users and man ers (providers of intermediate goods for larger
enterprises)
- linkages between training and acquisition of new technology
