SUPERVISION PLAN
1.    Bank Supervision Input into Key Activities. The staff input in the table below is in addition to
regular supervision needs for the review of progress reports, procurement actions, correspondence, etc.
(estimated for this project to require 15 weeks for the first year. 12 staff-weeks per year during the next
three project years, and 8 staff-weeks per year thereafter). The supervision of each component, including
review of procurement decisions and of progress reports, will be carried out by the task manager and
procurement specialist of the sector concerned under the responsibility of AF2PH.
2.    Borrower's Contribution to Supervision:
a.    Progress Reports are to be submitted in mid-February and mid-August each year by the
Project Coordinator at MRTT&T/DAT/ATU which will coordinate report preparation by the
various project agencies.
b.    Project monitoring and coordination will be the responsibility of the Project Coordinator at
MRTT&T/DAT/ATU. An implementation review workshop with the participation of the
various project agencies will be held in mid-February every year, convened by the
Coordinator.
c.    The Coordinator will be responsible for coordinating arrangements for Bank supervision
mission, dnd for providing information required by missions. Missions will normally be
accompanied by senior staff of MRTT&T. MRTT&T will be informed in advance which
project components will be covered during a mission, and representatives from the
implementing units of this Ministry will normally accompany the mission.
d.    Mission briefing meetings on arrival and wrap-up meeting3 will normally be chaired by the
Permanent Secretary of MRTT&T, with the participation of the Project Coordinator, and the
heads of the project implementing units of MRTT&T and the participating agencies.

REPUBLIC OF KENYA
MICRO-AND SMALL ENTERPRISE TRAINING AND TECHNOLOGY PROJECT
PROJECT IMPACT EVALUATION
1.01   Objecives and tasks. The objective of the evaluation is to assess the impact of project
interventions on the participants in terms of employment, earnings, and productivity. Analysis will focus
on evaluating efficiency and cost-effectiveness of three different components of the project: training,
technology, and infrastructure. It would also aim to compare the relative effectiveness of different types
of interventions in each component: (a) different implementation modalities of training and technology
components -voucher system and contract scheme for the training component and study tours, research
grants, exhibitions, and products catalogues for the technology component; and (b) alternative types of
land tenure -individual ownership, collective ownership through Jua Kali Associations and trusts,
respectively. The analyses should be designed to yield concrete recommendations for choosing the
appropriate models for the development of the informal sector in future.
Evaluation of Training Fund
1.02   Training fund evaluation is intended to evaluate the impact of the micro- and small enterprise
training fund component on trainees' income/wage and productivity. Design of the evaluation of
individual participants in the training fund should take into account the following considerations:
a.    A range of employment outcomes would be evaluated for individuals. These would
nclude (but not limited to) monthly income and hourly wage, hours worked per week
and job stability.
b.    To obtain unbiased assessment, a control group would be used in the evaluation.
Selection bias in measurement of the impacts of the project arises because the participants
are not a random sample of the informal sector entrepreneurs. This is due to the fact that
the trainees are selected on a competitive basis in the project. An effort would be made
to address the selection bias issue in the analyses.
c.    Three different methods would be adopted to evaluate the outcomes of individual
participants. One method is to compare post-training outcomes to pre-training measures
of the same individual or that of a control group of individuals in the informal sector.
This method recognizes the individuals being heterogeneous in terms of unmeasured
ability, tastes and motivation. A second method is to use a control group with similar
attributes to the trainee population. This technique uses program selection criteria to
identify an eligible group of non-trainees. A third method is to correct for the sample
selection using a two-stage econometric technique in which outcomes are measured
conditional upon selection into training. To the extent possible, the sensitivity of results
using the various methods should be compared.
d.    A methodology to assess the cost-effectiveness of the taining program would be
developed. Alternative modalities and delivery systems in each type of intervention
would also be evaluated to assess their relative efficacy. This approach would allow one
to tell whether outcomes vary on the basis of the participant's characteristics and type of



148
ANNEX 19
Page 2 of 3
intervention.
Evaluaton of Technology and Infastructure
1.03   This analysis would aim to evaluate the impacts of technology and infrastructure on the
productivity and employment generation of the small and micro-enterprises. The evaluation (particularly
of infrastructure component) would consider the following points:
a.    The impact of the project would be measured by comparing outcomes against the pre-
intervention measures of the same enterprise or that of a control group of enterprises.
The alternative measures would be compared to see if they lead to different conclusions.
b.    Cost-effectiveness would be assessed for the three different interventions in the
infrastructure component (two in this project and one in the GTZ/Belgium project):
individual ownership, collective ownership through Jua Kali Association and trustee,
respectively. Cost-benefit estimates can be sensitive to assumptions about both benefits
and costs, and accordingly, would be assessed for a variety of assumptions. It would be
ensured that a methodology to assess the process -the construction, distribution, and
management of the infrastructure- would be developed.
c.    Both quantitative and qualitative outcomes would be measured. The quantitative impacts
would include the increased production (or sales), employment, labor productivity. The
qualitative impacts would include better product quality, systems for accounting and
identification of new products and markets.
sureys
1.04   The evaluation described above requires the development of data bases. Two different types of
surveys will be designed for individual informal sector workers/entrepreneurs and enterprises. These
surveys include retrospective surveys and control group survey.
1.05   Survey of Individual Entrepreneurs. This survey would elicit the infornation on the
individual/household characteristics, work history and the characteristics of the enterprises which the
respondent owns or is an employee of. These data will be collected for both pre- and post-intervention.
More specifically, the following variables will be included:
a.    Worker Characteristics: These include age, gender, marital status (and dependents),
years of educational attaimment, highest level of education completed (date), skills and
vocational trainmg including the types of training in this project.
b.    Work History: These include data on work experience, attributes of the current employer
such as indubtry and firm size, years of tenure, occupation, and compensation (wages,
non-wage benefits and bonuses).
c.    Characteristics of Enterprises: These would include size, date established, sources of



149
ANNEX 19
Page 3 of 3
financing, type of building, accounting system, equipment, sales and profit, inventories,
breakdown of expenditures, suppliers, clients, work schedules, characteristics of paid
workers and of unpaid workers, including prior experience and training.
1.06   Samples of the project participants would be collected at least one year after the completion of
the program. A retrospective survey of participants would be conducted in 1995 for the 1994 cohort of
participants. The 1995 survey would be administered to a sample of the participants that is representative
of both training modalities; it would cover at least 10% of the men and women who comrleted training
in 1994 (about 600 individuals). This survey would limit coverage of the post-intervention period to
about one year. While it would be desirable to monitor the participants over a longer period, it is
difficult and costly in practice. A second survey would be fielded in 1996 to a similar sample size of the
participants completing the program in 1995. A third survey, possibly modified to address specific issues
that may arise during the implementation, could be fielded in 1998.
1.07   Survey of Nicro/Small Enterprises.  This survey would elicit basic information on
employment, earnings, training, financing and cost patterns in small- and microenterprises (besides
detailed information on their participation in the project). More specifically, these would include size,
date established, sources of financing, type of building, accounting system, equipment, sales and profit,
inventories, breakdown of expenditures, suppliers, clients, work schedules, characteristics of paid workers
and of unpaid workers, including prior experience and training. The survey will be conducted in a
manner similar to the retrospective survey for informal sector individuals as presented above.
1.08   Control Group Survey. A control group would be developed among informal sector enterprises
and entrepreneurs which have the characteristics comparable to those participating in the project which
are covered in the two surveys. In principle, such a group may be selected from the informal sector
entrepreneurs in the annual Small-Scale Business Enterprises Survey (SSBES) conducted by the CBS.
The variables similar to these surveys would be collected for a control group. The modifications of the
questions in the SSBES would thus be required to make two surveys comparable, thereby calling for the
coordination with the CBS.
